## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, time t, and velocity v, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillator. Typical models decompose dv_dt into restoring-force terms in x, damping terms in v, and optional time-dependent forcing/parametric excitation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (simple harmonic) oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration; sign of c0 typically negative for stability)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity plus linear stiffness)
- Constant + linear oscillator bias: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v (gravity/offset force plus linear stiffness and damping)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (approximate sign(v) friction using smooth tanh)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic drag where force scales with v|v|)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity with damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring nonlinearity)
- Piecewise/soft saturation stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (restoring force saturates at large |x|)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (velocity feedback where effective damping depends on amplitude)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (damping changes with speed; can create self-oscillation)
- Liénard-type polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (general nonlinear stiffness + amplitude-dependent damping)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic drive added to restoring/damping dynamics)
- Mathieu / parametric excitation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-periodic stiffness leading to parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear coupling of state variables: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x * v (state-dependent damping/feedback coupling)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (interpretable as dv_dt = -dU/dx + damping with U(x) polynomial)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Stable restoring forces often appear as odd functions of x (e.g., c*x, c*x**3), reflecting symmetry of many oscillators about x=0.
- Damping is typically odd in v (e.g., c*v, v*Abs(v), (c+v**2)*v), ensuring energy dissipation for v→-v symmetry.
- Hardening vs softening springs correspond to the sign of the cubic stiffness term in x**3, changing frequency with amplitude.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior is suggested by amplitude-dependent damping terms like (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v where damping can switch sign with |x|.
- Dry friction shows up as non-smooth sign-like dependence on v; smooth surrogates include tanh(c*v) or v/sqrt(v^2+c).
- Periodic forcing typically enters additively as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t), producing driven resonance when the drive frequency matches the natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when the coefficient multiplying x is time-periodic, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x.
- Energy-conserving dynamics (no damping/forcing) tend to depend on x only (dv_dt = f(x)); the presence of v terms indicates non-conservative effects.
- Cross terms like x*v indicate state-dependent damping/feedback or coordinate-dependent dissipation commonly used in phenomenological oscillator models.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO20)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1) - c2*beta*v - mu*(c3 - v**c4)*v - omega0**c5*(gamma*Abs(v)**c6 + c7)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

Let \(G(x,v)\) denote the GT (no \(t\) dependence):
\[
G= -0.0441723168923102\,v^3\;-\;0.333481093540657\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;1.24947480809752\,v\;-\;3.58220621454007\,x\big(0.0479281989045915|v|^{1/3}+1\big)\;-\;0.624737404048761\log(|v|+1).
\]
Expand the polynomial-in-\(v\) part:
\[
-0.33348\,v(1-v^2)= -0.33348\,v +0.33348\,v^3.
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
G = A\,v^3 + B\,v + C\,\log(|v|+1) + x\,(D\,|v|^{1/3}+E),
\]
with **no** terms like \(x|v|\), \(vx\), \(v^{c}x\) (unless \(c=0\) giving just \(x\)), no \(x\log(\cdot)\), no constants, no \(t\)-sinusoids, etc. Concretely:
- \(A = 0.333481093540657 - 0.0441723168923102 = 0.2893087766483468\)
- \(B = -0.333481093540657 - 1.24947480809752 = -1.582955901638177\)
- \(C = -0.624737404048761\)
- \(E = -3.58220621454007\)
- \(D = -3.58220621454007\cdot 0.0479281989045915 \approx -0.1717\) (exact product not needed; it’s nonzero)
and the \(x\)-dependent nonlinearity is \(x|v|^{1/3}\) (not \(x|v|\), not \(x\log\), not \(x v^p\) without absolute value).

A candidate can match only if it can reproduce **both**:
1) \(\log(|v|+1)\) with coefficient \(C\), and  
2) the \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term plus the linear \(-3.5822\,x\), **without introducing extra functional forms**.

Now check each candidate.

---

### 1. \(c0*x + c1*v + c2*v^3 + c3*\log(c4|v|+1) + c5*x*\log(c6|v|+1) + c7*v^{c8}*x\)
- Has needed \(x\), \(v\), \(v^3\), \(\log(\cdot)\).
- But GT needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Candidate’s only nonlinear-in-\(v\) times \(x\) is \(x v^{c8}\) **without Abs**. Because \(v\) can be negative, \(v^{1/3}\) is not equal to \(|v|^{1/3}\) (it changes sign). No other term can create \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
- Also must kill \(x\log(\cdot)\) by setting \(c5=0\) (fine), but still cannot create \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
⇒ Not match.

### 2. Same as (1) + \(c9\)
- GT has no additive constant; could set \(c9=0\).
- Still fails for same reason: cannot produce \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
⇒ Not match.

### 3. Like (1) but \(c7*x*(c8+v)^{c9}\)
- To get \(|v|^{1/3}\) you’d need an absolute value; \((c8+v)^{c9}\) cannot equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\) (also shift breaks symmetry).
⇒ Not match.

### 4. \(c0*v + c1*x|v| + c2*v^3 + c3\log(c4|v|+1) + c5*x + c6*v^{c7}x + c8*v|v| + x\)
- Contains \(x|v|\) and \(v|v|\) which GT does not have; can set \(c1=0,c8=0\).

⇒ Not match.

⇒ Not match.

- Still cannot form \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
⇒ Not match.

- Same as (4): cannot form \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
⇒ Not match.

⇒ Not match.
